{'item 1. ': 'Business Company Background Apple Computer, Inc. ("Apple" the "Company") was incorporated under the laws the State California January , . The Company designs, manufactures and markets personal computers and related software, peripherals and personal computing and communicating solutions. The Company\' products include the Macintosh® line desktop and notebook computers, the Mac ® operating system, the iPod\x99 digital music player, and portfolio software and peripheral products for education, creative, consumer and business customers. The Company sells its products through its online stores, direct sales force, third-party wholesalers and resellers, and its own retail stores. The Company\' fiscal year ends the last Saturday September. Unless otherwise stated, all information presented this Form - based the Company\' fiscal calendar. Business Strategy Digital Hub Apple committed bringing the best possible personal computing experience students, educators, creative professionals, businesses and consumers around the world through its innovative hardware, software, peripherals and Internet offerings, including Mac\x99 and the iTunes® Music Store\x99. The Company believes that personal computing has entered new era which the personal computer functions for both professionals and consumers the digital hub for advanced new digital devices such the Company\' iPod digital music players, personal digital assistants, cellular phones, digital still and movie cameras, and DVD players, and other electronic devices. The attributes the personal computer, including its ability run complex applications, possess high quality user interface, contain large and relatively inexpensive storage, and easily connect the Internet multiple ways and varying speeds, can individually add value these devices and interconnect them well. Apple the only company the personal computer industry that designs and manufactures the entire personal computer\x97from the hardware and operating system sophisticated applications. Apple provides innovative industrial design, intuitive ease- -use, and built- networking, graphics, and multimedia capabilities. Thus, the Company uniquely positioned offer digital hub products and solutions. Apple develops products and technologies that adhere many industry standards order provide optimized user experience through interoperability with peripherals and devices from other companies. Apple has played role the development, enhancement, promotion, and use numerous these industry standards, many which are discussed below. Hardware Products The Company offers range personal computing products including desktop and notebook personal computers, related devices and peripherals, networking and connectivity products, and various third-party hardware products. All the Company\' Macintosh products utilize PowerPC® RISC-based microprocessors. The Company\' entire line Macintosh systems, excluding servers, features the Company\' suite software for digital photography, music, and movies. Power Mac® The Power Mac line desktop personal computers targeted business and professional users and designed meet the speed, expansion and networking needs the most demanding Macintosh user. Powered the PowerPC processor, designed IBM and Apple, and featuring GHz front-side bus and the ability address 8GB memory, the current Power Mac utilizes -bit processing technology for advanced -bit computation, while running existing -bit applications natively. The PowerPC processor architecture based completely new execution core that features massively parallel computation, full symmetric multi-processing, two double precision floating point units and optimized Velocity Engine\x99. Power Mac systems, encased professional aluminum enclosure with computer controlled cooling for quiet operation, also include all models SuperDrive - DVD- drives, digital audio and PCI- expansion, and advanced input and output technologies including Gigabit Ethernet, FireWire® and USB ports. The system also supports Mbps AirPort Extreme® wireless networking and Bluetooth ready for wireless connections host Bluetooth-enabled peripherals. Prior the availability the Power Mac August , the Company\' Power Mac line during most fiscal featured PowerPC processors all models. The Company continues offer Power Macintosh system with single dual Ghz processor configuration. Xserve® and Xserve RAID Storage System Xserve, the Company\' first ever rack-mount server product, was designed for simple setup and remote management intensive input output ( ) applications such digital video, high-resolution digital imagery, and large databases. February , the Company upgraded its Xserve rack servers with more powerful processors, more storage capacity, and FireWire interface. the same time, the Company introduced the Xserve RAID Storage System, rack storage system that holds hot-swapable drive modules capable holding terabytes data. Xserve RAID architecture combines affordable, high-capacity ATA drive technology with Fibre Channel interface for reliable and fast data access. Xserve RAID provides RAID level throughput that supports affordable real-time high definition ( ) 1080i video editing. PowerBook ® The PowerBook family portable computers designed meet the mobile computing needs professionals and advanced consumer users. The -inch PowerBook features -inch wide-format active-matrix display, encased durable aluminum alloy enclosure, -inch thick, and weighs little pounds. The -inch PowerBook also features built- support for AirPort Extreme Mbps 11g wireless networking, new high-speed FireWire , backlit keyboard with ambient light sensors, and built- Bluetooth for wireless connection cell phones and other Bluetooth equipped peripherals. The -inch PowerBook features -inch, active-matrix display housed lightweight, durable aluminum alloy enclosure weighing approximately pounds. Operating System Software During , the Company introduced the first customer release its new client operating system, Mac , and its first significant upgrade, Mac version . its introduction, Mac offered advanced functionality built open-source UNIX-based foundation and incorporated the most fundamental changes both core technology and user interface design made the Company the Mac single upgrade since the original introduction the Macintosh . Mac features memory protection, pre-emptive multi-tasking, and symmetric multiprocessing. Mac includes Apple\' Quartz\x99® graphics engine (based the Internet-standard Portable Document Format) for enhanced graphics and broad font support, OpenGL for enhanced graphics and gaming, and Apple\' new user interface named "Aqua ® ," which combines superior ease- -use with new functionality. January , the Company made Mac the default operating system all new Macintosh systems. August , the Company introduced Mac version (code named "Jaguar"), the second significant upgrade the original Mac version. Jaguar included new Mail application designed manage junk mail; iChat, AIM-compatible instant messenger; system-wide Address Book; Inkwell\x99 handwriting recognition; improved Universal Access; enhanced Finder\x99; updated version QuickTime®, the Company\' multimedia software for playing, interacting with viewing video, audio, and graphics files; and updated version Sherlock®, the Company\' advanced Internet search engine. Jaguar also featured accelerated graphics performance, increased compatibility with Windows networks, and UNIX-based foundation with enhancements including FreeBSD and GCC -based developer tools. October , the Company released Mac version (code named "Panther"), the Company\' current version Mac . Panther incorporates more than new features including completely new Finder\x99; Exposé, new way organize windows and instantly see all open windows once; FileVault\x99, new feature that secures the contents home directory with -bit AES encryption; iChat , complete desktop video conferencing solution; and enhanced support for use Windows-based networks. Apple Remote Desktop\x99 for Mac software enables users, teachers and administrators remotely manage other Macintosh systems anywhere local network, AirPort ® wireless network across the Internet. With Apple Remote Desktop, teachers can view students\' computer screens, perform group demonstrations and help individuals with real-time screen-sharing, text chat and the "request attention" command. System administrators can provide remote assistance, get comprehensive system profiles, reconfigure system settings and quickly and easily distribute software applications across hundreds computers\x97all from one central location over both Ethernet and AirPort wireless networks. Apple Remote Desktop supports multiple levels administrator access, each with its own password, providing secure way for teachers department-level administrators assist users while restricting privileges for deleting items changing system settings. The Company\' Rendezvous\x99 networking technology based open Internet Engineering Task Force (IETF) Standard Protocols such , ARP and DNS. Rendezvous uses industry standard networking protocols and zero configuration technology automatically discover and connect devices over any network, including Ethernet -based wireless networks like the Company\' AirPort product. Major developers such Canon, Epson, Hewlett-Packard, Lexmark, Philips, Sybase, World Book and Xerox have announced support for Rendezvous broad range products including network printers, consumer electronics, enterprise database management and educational applications. The Company has made the Rendezvous source code freely available allowing developers use Rendezvous technology their network-enabled devices software applications. The Rendezvous source code includes software support UNIX, Linux, and Windows-based systems and devices. Rendezvous support built into Mac . The Company developed FireWire ® technology, also referred IEEE , which high-speed serial technology for connecting digital devices such digital camcorders and cameras desktop and portable computers. With its high data-transfer speed and "hot plug-and-play" capability, FireWire has become established cross-platform industry standard for both consumers and professionals and the data interface choice for today\' digital video and audio devices, well external hard drives and other high-speed peripherals. Markets and Distribution The Company\' customers are primarily the education, creative, consumer, and business markets. Certain customers are attracted Macintosh computers for variety reasons, including the reduced amount training resulting from the Macintosh computer\' intuitive ease use, advanced graphics capabilities, industrial design features the Company\' hardware products, and ability Macintosh computers network and communicate with other computer systems and environments. Competition The Company confronted aggressive competition all areas its business. The market for the design, manufacture, and sale personal computers and related software and peripheral products highly competitive. This market continues characterized rapid technological advances both hardware and software development, which have substantially increased the capabilities and applications these products, and have resulted the frequent introduction new products and significant price, feature, and performance competition. Over the past several years, price competition the market for personal computers has been particularly intense. The Company\' competitors who sell personal computers based other operating systems have aggressively cut prices and lowered their product margins gain maintain market share. The Company\' results operations and financial condition have been, and the future may continue , adversely affected these and other industry-wide downward pressures gross margins. The principal competitive factors the market for personal computers include relative price performance, product quality and reliability, design innovation, availability software, product features, marketing and distribution capability, service and support, availability hardware peripherals, and corporate reputation. Further, the personal computer industry and its customers place more reliance the Internet, increasing number Internet devices that are smaller, simpler, and less expensive than traditional personal computers may compete for market share with the Company\' existing products. The Company currently taking and will continue take steps respond the competitive pressures being placed its personal computer sales result innovations competing platforms. The Company\' future operating results and financial condition are substantially dependent its ability continue develop improvements the Macintosh platform order maintain perceived functional and design advantages over competing platforms. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products ( ., hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition Financial Statements . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped, and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the United States, and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]DI1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed and determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end-user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Future market conditions and product transitions may require the Company increase customer incentive programs and incur incremental price protection obligations that could result additional reductions revenue the time such programs are offered. Additionally, certain customer incentive programs require management estimate the number customers who will actually redeem the incentive based historical experience and the specific terms and conditions particular incentive programs. greater than estimated proportion customers redeem such incentives, the Company would required record additional reductions revenue, which could have material adverse impact the Company\' results operations. Allowance for Doubtful Accounts The Company distributes its products through third-party resellers and directly certain education, consumer, and commercial customers. The Company generally does not require collateral from its customers. However, when possible the Company does attempt limit credit risk trade receivables with credit insurance for certain customers Latin America, Europe and Asia and arranging with third-party financing companies provide flooring arrangements and other loan and lease programs the Company\' direct customers. These credit-financing arrangements are directly between the third-party financing company and the end customer. such, the Company does not assume any recourse credit risk sharing related any these arrangements. However, considerable trade receivables that are not covered collateral, third-party flooring arrangements, credit insurance are outstanding with the Company\' distribution and retail channel partners. The allowance for doubtful accounts based management\' assessment the collectibility specific customer accounts and includes consideration the credit worthiness and financial condition those specific customers. The Company records allowance reduce the specific receivables the amount that reasonably believed collectible. The Company also records allowance for all other trade receivables based multiple factors including historical experience with bad debts, the general economic environment, the financial condition the Company\' distribution channels, and the aging such receivables. there deterioration major customer\' financial condition, the Company becomes aware additional information related the credit worthiness major customer, future actual default rates trade receivables general differ from those currently anticipated, the Company may have adjust its allowance for doubtful accounts, which would affect earnings the period the adjustments are made. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, further discussed Part , Item this Form - Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation , requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. The FASB decided April , require all companies expense the value employee stock options. Companies will required measure the cost employee stock options according their fair value. The FASB has indicated that plans issue the first quarter calendar year exposure draft new accounting standard addressing this matter. Prior issuance this exposure draft, the FASB has indicated will addressing several significant technical issues. Among other things, the FASB must determine the extent which the new accounting standard will permit adjustments recognized expense for actual option forfeitures and actual performance outcomes. This determination will affect the timing and amount compensation expense recognized. Also, method determine the fair value employee stock options must established. Current accounting standards require use option-pricing model, such the Black-Scholes formula, determine fair value and provide guidance adjusting some the input factors used the model. This valuation approach has received significant criticism and may subject changes that could have significant impact the calculated fair value employee stock options under the new standard. the Company\' annual shareholder\' meeting April , , shareholders approved proposal requesting that the Company\' Board Directors (the Board) establish policy expensing the value all future employee stock options issued the Company. The Board and management appreciate and take seriously the views expressed the Company\' shareholders. discussed the Company\' Form - for the period ended March , , the Company had decided not expense the value employee stock options until the FASB finalizes its new accounting standard the matter. The Company based this decision the FASB\' announced intention soon require all companies expense the value employee stock options and the FASB\' near-term review technical issues that will play significant role determining the fair value and accounting for employee stock options. The Company monitors progress the FASB and other developments with respect the general issue employee stock compensation. the future, should the Company expense the value employee stock options, either out choice due new requirements issued the FASB, the Company may have recognize substantially more compensation expense future periods that could have material adverse impact the Company\' future results operations. ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]DY1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' THIS THE END COMPOSITION COMPONENT TOC_END NOTES CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS Note \x97Summary Significant Accounting Policies Apple Computer, Inc. and its subsidiaries (the Company) designs, manufactures and markets personal computers and related software, peripherals and personal computing and communicating solutions. The Company\' products include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the Mac operating system, the iPod digital music player, and portfolio software products and peripherals for education, creative, consumer and business customers. The Company sells its products through its online stores, direct sales force, third-party wholesalers and resellers, and its own retail stores. Basis Presentation and Preparation The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts the Company. Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. The preparation these consolidated financial statements conformity with . generally accepted accounting principles requires management make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported these consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior year amounts the consolidated financial statements and notes thereto have been reclassified conform the current year presentation. Typically, the Company\' fiscal year ends the last Saturday September. Fiscal years , and were each -week years. However, approximately every six years, the Company reports -week fiscal year align its fiscal quarters with calendar quarters adding week its first fiscal quarter. All information presented herein based the Company\' fiscal calendar. Financial Instruments Cash Equivalents and Short-term Investments The Company places its short-term investments highly liquid securities issued high credit quality issuers. All highly liquid investments with maturities three months less the date purchase are classified cash equivalents; highly liquid investments with maturities greater than three months are classified short-term investments. Management determines the appropriate classification its investments debt and marketable equity securities the time purchase and reevaluates such designation each balance sheet date. The Company\' debt and marketable equity securities have been classified and accounted for available-for-sale. These securities are carried fair value, with the unrealized gains and losses, net taxes, reported component shareholders\' equity. The cost securities sold based upon the specific identification method. Non-Current Debt and Equity Investments The Company has made investments non-current debt and equity investments public and privately held companies that have been reflected the consolidated balance sheets long-term assets within other assets. They are not categorized current assets either because, given their nature, they are not readily convertible into cash because they represent potentially longer-term investments the Company. Further, the fair value these investments has been subject high degree volatility. The Company\' non-current debt and equity investments have been categorized available-for-sale requiring that they carried fair value with unrealized gains and losses, net taxes, reported equity component accumulated other comprehensive income. However, the Company recognizes impairment charge earnings the event decline fair value below the cost basis one these investments determined other-than-temporary. The Company includes recognized gains and losses resulting from the sale from other-than-temporary declines fair value associated with these investments other income and expense. Occasionally, the Company uses short-term equity derivatives ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]EA1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' manage potential dispositions non-current debt and equity investments. Any gains losses associated with such derivatives are recognized currently other income and expense. Financial Instruments with Characteristics Both Liabilities and Equity May , , the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued Statement Financial Accounting Standards (SFAS) . , Accounting for Certain Financial Instruments with Characteristics Both Liabilities and Equity . SFAS . requires issuers classify liabilities ( assets some circumstances) certain freestanding financial instruments that embody obligations for the issuer and have characteristics both liabilities and equity. The Company adopted the provisions SFAS . June , , which resulted favorable cumulative-effect type adjustment approximately $ million. This adjustment related forward purchase agreement that allowed the Company acquire million shares its common stock average price $ per share for total cost $ million. The Company settled this forward purchase agreement August , which resulted additional gain approximately $ million representing the increase fair value the agreement from June , through the settlement date. Inventories Inventories are stated the lower cost (first- , first-out) market. the cost the inventories exceeds their market value, provisions are made currently for the difference between the cost and the market value. Property, Plant, and Equipment Property, plant, and equipment are stated cost. Depreciation computed use the declining balance and straight-line methods over the estimated useful lives the assets, which are years for buildings, from years for equipment, and the shorter lease terms years for leasehold improvements. The Company capitalizes eligible costs acquire develop internal-use software that are incurred subsequent the preliminary project stage. Capitalized costs related internal-use software are amortized using the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives the assets, which range from years. Asset Retirement Obligations September , , the Company adopted SFAS . , Accounting for Asset Retirement Obligations , which addresses financial accounting and reporting for obligations associated with the retirement tangible long-lived assets and the associated asset retirement costs. The standard applies legal obligations associated with the retirement long-lived assets that result from the acquisition, construction, development and normal use the assets. SFAS . requires that the fair value liability for asset retirement obligation recognized the period which incurred reasonable estimate fair value can made. The fair value the liability added the carrying amount the associated asset and this additional carrying amount depreciated over the life the asset. All the Company\' existing asset retirement obligations are associated with commitments return property subject operating leases original condition upon lease termination. The Company estimated that September , , gross expected future cash flows $ million would required fulfill these obligations. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products (hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition Financial Statements . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the United States, and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed and determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. Revenue from extended warranty and support contracts deferred and recognized ratably over the warranty and support periods. These contracts typically include extended phone support, certain repairs, web-based support resources, diagnostic tools, and extend the Company\' one-year basic limited parts and labor warranty. The Company sells software and peripheral products obtained from other companies. The Company establishes its own pricing and retains related inventory risk, the primary obligor sales transactions with its customers, and assumes the credit risk for amounts billed its customers. Accordingly, the Company recognizes revenue for the sale products obtained from other companies the gross amount billed. Revenue arrangements that include multiple elements such hardware, software, and services allocated each element based vendor specific objective evidence (VSOE) the fair value each element. Allocated revenue for each element recognized when revenue recognition criteria have been met for each element. VSOE determined based the price charged when each element sold separately. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Warranty Expense The Company provides currently for the estimated cost for product warranties the time the related revenue recognized. Research and Development Research and development costs are expensed incurred. Development costs computer software sold, leased otherwise marketed are subject capitalization beginning when product\' technological feasibility has been established and ending when product available for general release customers pursuant SFAS . , Computer Software Sold, Leased, Otherwise Marketed . most instances, the Company\' products are released soon after technological feasibility has been established. Therefore, costs incurred subsequent achievement technological feasibility are usually not significant, and generally all software development costs have been expensed. During the third and fourth quarters , the Company incurred substantial development costs associated with the development Mac version (code-named "Panther"), which enhances the features and functionality the previous version Mac , subsequent achievement technological feasibility evidenced public demonstration and release developer beta June , and prior release the final version the product the first quarter . Therefore, during the Company capitalized approximately $ million development costs associated with the development Panther. Amortization this asset began the first quarter when Panther was shipped and being recognized straight-line basis accordance with SFAS . over year estimated useful life. Amortization this asset began the fourth quarter when Jaguar was shipped and being recognized straight-line basis accordance with SFAS . over year estimated useful life. addition, during , the Company also began capitalizing certain costs related development its new PowerSchool enterprise student information system. Capitalization approximately $ million began upon achievement technological feasibility the first quarter . The final version the enterprise student information system was released July . During the Company incurred substantial development costs associated with the development the original version Mac , subsequent release public beta version the product and prior release the final product version. result, the Company capitalized approximately $ million development costs during associated with development Mac . Restructuring Charges June , the FASB issued SFAS . , Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit Disposal Activities . SFAS . supersedes Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) Issue . - , Liability Recognition for Certain Employee Termination Benefits and Other Costs Exit Activity (Including Certain Costs Associated with Restructuring) and requires that liability for cost associated with exit disposal activity recognized when the liability incurred, opposed when management commits exit plan. SFAS . also establishes that the liability should initially measured and recorded fair value. This Statement was effective for exit disposal activities initiated after December , . The provisions SFAS . were required applied prospectively after the adoption date newly initiated exit activities. Stock-Based Compensation The Company measures compensation expense for its employee stock-based compensation plans using the intrinsic value method prescribed Accounting Principles Board (APB) Opinion . , Accounting for Stock Issued Employees. The Company applies the disclosure provisions SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation , amended SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation\x97Transition and Disclosure the fair value-based method had been applied measuring compensation expense. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, discussed below, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. required under SFAS . , the pro forma effects stock-based compensation net income and earnings per common share for employee stock options granted and employee stock purchase plan purchases have been estimated the date grant and beginning the period, respectively, using Black-Scholes option pricing model. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. The Black-Scholes option valuation model was developed for use estimating the fair value freely traded options that have vesting restrictions and are fully transferable. addition, option valuation models require the input highly subjective assumptions including the expected life options and the Company\' expected stock price volatility. Because the Company\' employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares have characteristics significantly different from those freely traded options, and because changes the subjective input assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate, ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]EA1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' management\' opinion, the existing models not provide reliable measure the fair value the Company\' employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income (loss) over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. Comprehensive Income Comprehensive income consists two components, net income and other comprehensive income. Other comprehensive income refers revenue, expenses, gains and losses that under generally accepted accounting principles are recorded element shareholders\' equity but are excluded from net income. The Company\' other comprehensive income comprised foreign currency translation adjustments from those subsidiaries not using the . dollar their functional currency, unrealized gains and losses marketable securities categorized available-for-sale, and net deferred gains and losses certain derivative instruments accounted for cash flow hedges. Information about the Company\' products, major customers, and geographic areas company-wide basis also disclosed. Foreign Exchange Risk Management The Company enters into foreign currency forward and option contracts with financial institutions primarily protect against foreign exchange risk associated with existing assets and liabilities, certain firmly committed transactions and certain probable but not firmly committed transactions. Generally, the Company\' practice hedge majority its existing material foreign exchange transaction exposures. However, the Company may not hedge certain foreign exchange transaction exposures due immateriality, prohibitive economic cost hedging particular exposures, limited availability appropriate hedging instruments. Interest Rate Risk Management The Company sometimes enters into interest rate derivative transactions, including interest rate swaps, collars, and floors, with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income its cash equivalents and short-term investments with its fixed-rate interest expense its long-term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short-term . interest rates. September , , the Company had entered into interest rate swaps with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income its cash equivalents and short-term investments with its fixed-rate interest expense its long-term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short-term . interest rates. Contingencies Beginning September , , three shareholder class action lawsuits were filed the United States District Court for the Northern District California against the Company and its Chief Executive Officer. These lawsuits are substantially identical, and purport bring suit behalf persons who purchased the Company\' publicly traded common stock between July , , and September , . The complaints allege violations the Securities Exchange Act and seek unspecified compensatory damages and other relief. The Company believes these claims are without merit and intends defend them vigorously. The Company filed motion dismiss June , , which was heard the Court September , . December , , the Court granted the Company\' motion dismiss for failure state cause action, with leave Plaintiffs amend their complaint within thirty days. Plaintiffs filed their amended complaint January , , and March , , the Company filed motion dismiss the amended complaint. The Court heard the Company\' motion July , and dismissed Plaintiff\' claims with prejudice August , . Plaintiffs have appealed the ruling. The Company subject certain other legal proceedings and claims that have arisen the ordinary course business and have not been fully adjudicated. the opinion management, the Company does not have potential liability related any current legal proceedings and claims that would individually the aggregate have material adverse effect its financial condition, liquidity results operations. However, the results legal proceedings cannot predicted with certainty. Should the Company fail prevail any these legal matters should several these legal matters resolved against the Company the same reporting period, the operating results particular reporting period could materially adversely affected. Note \x97Segment Information and Geographic Data The Company manages its business primarily geographic basis. The Company\' reportable segments are comprised the Americas, Europe, Japan, and Retail. The Americas segment includes both North and South America, except for the activities the Company\' Retail segment. The Europe segment includes European countries well the Middle East and Africa. The Japan segment includes only Japan. September , , the Retail segment currently operates Apple-owned retail stores the United States. Other operating segments include Asia-Pacific, which includes Australia and Asia except for Japan, and the Company\' subsidiary, Filemaker, Inc. Each reportable operating segment provides similar hardware and software products and similar services, and the accounting policies the various segments are the same those described the Summary Significant Accounting Policies Note , except described below for the Retail segment. The Company evaluates the performance its operating segments based net sales. The Retail segment\' performance also evaluated based operating income. Net sales for geographic segments are based the location the customers. Operating income for each segment includes net sales third parties, related cost sales, and operating expenses directly attributable the segment. Operating income for each segment excludes other income and expense and certain expenses that are managed outside the operating segments. Costs excluded from segment operating income include various corporate expenses, manufacturing costs not included standard costs, income taxes, and various nonrecurring charges. Corporate expenses include research and development, corporate marketing expenses, and other separately managed general and administrative expenses including certain corporate expenses associated with support the Retail segment. The Company does not include intercompany transfers between segments for management reporting purposes. Segment assets exclude corporate assets. Corporate assets include cash, short-term and long-term investments, manufacturing facilities, miscellaneous corporate infrastructure, goodwill and other acquired intangible assets, and retail store construction- -progress that not subject depreciation. Except for the Retail segment, capital expenditures for long-lived assets are not reported management segment. Capital expenditures the Retail segment were $ million, $ million, and $ million , , and , respectively. Operating income for all segments except Retail includes cost sales standard cost. Board Committees The Board has standing Compensation Committee, Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee (" Nominating Committee" ) and Audit and Finance Committee (" Audit Committee "). The Compensation Committee primarily responsible for reviewing the compensation arrangements for the Company\' executive officers, including the Chief Executive Officer, and for administering the Company\' stock option plans. Members the Compensation Committee are Messrs. Campbell, Drexler, Gore and . Levinson. The Nominating Committee assists the Board identifying qualified individuals become directors, determines the composition the Board and its committees, monitors the process assess Board effectiveness and helps develop and implement the Company\' corporate governance guidelines. Members the Nominating Committee are Messrs. Campbell, Drexler, Gore and . Levinson. The Audit Committee primarily responsible for overseeing the services performed the Company\' independent auditors and internal audit department, evaluating the Company\' accounting policies and its system internal controls and reviewing significant financial transactions. Consistent with the Nasdaq audit committee structure and membership requirements, the Audit Committee comprised three members: Messrs. Campbell, York and . Levinson. Because . York\' affiliation with MicroWarehouse, (see Item . Certain Relationships and Related Transactions), deemed "non-independent" director. permitted under the Nasdaq requirements, the Board carefully considered . York\' affiliation with MicroWarehouse well his accounting and financial expertise and determined that the best interest the Company and its shareholders that continue serve member the Audit Committee. Both . Campbell and . Levinson are independent directors. The Audit, Compensation and Nominating Committees operate under written charters adopted the Board. These charters are available the Company\' website www apple com investor. Arrangements with Named Executive Officers Change Control Arrangements\x97Stock Options the event "change control" the Company, all outstanding options under the Company\' stock option plans, except the Director Plan, will, unless otherwise determined the plan administrator, become exercisable full, and will cashed out amount equal the difference between the applicable "change control price" and the exercise price. The Director Plan provides that upon "change control" the Company, all unvested options held non-employee directors will automatically become fully vested and exercisable and will cashed out amount equal the difference between the applicable "change control price" and the exercise price the options. "change control" under these plans generally defined ( ) the acquisition any person % more the combined voting power the Company\' outstanding securities ( ) the occurrence transaction requiring shareholder approval and involving the sale all substantially all the assets the Company the merger the Company with into another corporation. addition, options granted the Named Executive Officers generally provide that the event there "change control," defined the Company\' stock option plans, and connection with following such "change control," their employment terminated without "Cause" they should resign for "Good Reason," those options outstanding that are not yet vested and exercisable the date such "change control" shall become fully vested and exercisable. Generally, "Cause" defined include felony conviction, willful disclosure confidential information willful and continued failure perform his her employment duties. Critical Accounting Policies The preparation financial statements and related disclosures conformity with . generally accepted accounting principles and the Company\' discussion and analysis its financial condition and results operations requires the Company\' management make judgments, assumptions and estimates that affect the amounts reported its consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements Item this Form - describe the significant accounting policies and methods used the preparation the Company\' consolidated financial statements. Management bases its estimates historical experience and various other assumptions that believes reasonable under the circumstances, the results which form the basis for making judgments about the carrying values assets and liabilities. Actual results may differ from these estimates. Management believes the following critical accounting policies. That , they are both important the portrayal the Company\' financial condition and results, and they require management make judgments and estimates about matters that are inherently uncertain. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products ( ., hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition Financial Statements . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped, and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the United States, and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]DI1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed and determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end-user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Future market conditions and product transitions may require the Company increase customer incentive programs and incur incremental price protection obligations that could result additional reductions revenue the time such programs are offered. Additionally, certain customer incentive programs require management estimate the number customers who will actually redeem the incentive based historical experience and the specific terms and conditions particular incentive programs. greater than estimated proportion customers redeem such incentives, the Company would required record additional reductions revenue, which could have material adverse impact the Company\' results operations. Allowance for Doubtful Accounts The Company distributes its products through third-party resellers and directly certain education, consumer, and commercial customers. The Company generally does not require collateral from its customers. However, when possible the Company does attempt limit credit risk trade receivables with credit insurance for certain customers Latin America, Europe and Asia and arranging with third-party financing companies provide flooring arrangements and other loan and lease programs the Company\' direct customers. These credit-financing arrangements are directly between the third-party financing company and the end customer. such, the Company does not assume any recourse credit risk sharing related any these arrangements. However, considerable trade receivables that are not covered collateral, third-party flooring arrangements, credit insurance are outstanding with the Company\' distribution and retail channel partners. The allowance for doubtful accounts based management\' assessment the collectibility specific customer accounts and includes consideration the credit worthiness and financial condition those specific customers. The Company records allowance reduce the specific receivables the amount that reasonably believed collectible. The Company also records allowance for all other trade receivables based multiple factors including historical experience with bad debts, the general economic environment, the financial condition the Company\' distribution channels, and the aging such receivables. there deterioration major customer\' financial condition, the Company becomes aware additional information related the credit worthiness major customer, future actual default rates trade receivables general differ from those currently anticipated, the Company may have adjust its allowance for doubtful accounts, which would affect earnings the period the adjustments are made. Inventory Valuation and Inventory Purchase Commitments The Company must order components for its products and build inventory advance product shipments. The Company records write-down for inventories components and products, including third-party products held for resale, which have become obsolete are excess anticipated demand net realizable value. The Company performs detailed review inventory each period that considers multiple factors including demand forecasts, product lifecycle status, product development plans, current sales levels, and component cost trends. The personal computer industry subject rapid and unpredictable pace product and component obsolescence and demand changes. future demand market conditions for the Company\' products are less favorable than forecasted unforeseen technological changes negatively impact the utility component inventory, the Company may required ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]DI1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' record additional write-downs which would negatively affect gross margins the period when the write-downs are recorded. The Company accrues necessary reserves for cancellation fees related component orders that have been cancelled. Consistent with industry practice, the Company acquires components through combination formal purchase orders, supplier contracts, and open orders based projected demand information. These commitments typically cover the Company\' requirements for periods ranging from days. there abrupt and substantial decline demand for one more the Company\' products unanticipated change technological requirements for any the Company\' products, the Company may required record additional reserves for cancellation fees that would negatively affect gross margins the period when the cancellation fees are identified. Valuation Long-Lived Assets Including Acquired Intangibles The Company reviews property, plant, and equipment and certain identifiable intangible assets for impairment whenever events changes circumstances indicate the carrying amount such asset may not recoverable. Recoverability these assets measured comparison their carrying amount future undiscounted cash flows the assets are expected generate. such assets are considered impaired, the impairment recognized earnings equals the amount which the carrying value the assets exceeds their fair market value. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, further discussed Part , Item this Form - Note the Notes Consolidated Financial Statements, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation , requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. The FASB decided April , require all companies expense the value employee stock options. Companies will required measure the cost employee stock options according their fair value. The FASB has indicated that plans issue the first quarter calendar year exposure draft new accounting standard addressing this matter. Prior issuance this exposure draft, the FASB has indicated will addressing several significant technical issues. Among other things, the FASB must determine the extent which the new accounting standard will permit adjustments recognized expense for actual option forfeitures and actual performance outcomes. This determination will affect the timing and amount compensation expense recognized. Also, method determine the fair value employee stock options must established. Current accounting standards require use option-pricing model, such the Black-Scholes formula, determine fair value and provide guidance adjusting some the input factors used the model. This valuation approach has received significant criticism and may subject changes that could have significant impact the calculated fair value employee stock options under the new standard. the Company\' annual shareholder\' meeting April , , shareholders approved proposal requesting that the Company\' Board Directors (the Board) establish policy expensing the value all future employee stock options issued the Company. The Board and management appreciate and take seriously the views expressed the Company\' shareholders. discussed the Company\' Form - for the period ended March , , the Company had decided not expense the value employee stock options until the FASB finalizes its new accounting standard the matter. The Company based this decision the FASB\' announced intention soon require all companies expense the value employee stock options and the FASB\' near-term review technical issues that will play significant role determining the fair value and accounting for employee stock options. The Company monitors progress the FASB and other developments with respect the general issue employee stock compensation. the future, should the Company expense the value employee stock options, either out choice due new requirements issued the FASB, the Company may have recognize substantially more compensation expense future periods that could have material adverse impact the Company\' future results operations. ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]DY1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' THIS THE END COMPOSITION COMPONENT TOC_END NOTES CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS Note \x97Summary Significant Accounting Policies Apple Computer, Inc. and its subsidiaries (the Company) designs, manufactures and markets personal computers and related software, peripherals and personal computing and communicating solutions. The Company\' products include the Macintosh line desktop and notebook computers, the Mac operating system, the iPod digital music player, and portfolio software products and peripherals for education, creative, consumer and business customers. The Company sells its products through its online stores, direct sales force, third-party wholesalers and resellers, and its own retail stores. Basis Presentation and Preparation The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts the Company. Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. The preparation these consolidated financial statements conformity with . generally accepted accounting principles requires management make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported these consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior year amounts the consolidated financial statements and notes thereto have been reclassified conform the current year presentation. Typically, the Company\' fiscal year ends the last Saturday September. Fiscal years , and were each -week years. However, approximately every six years, the Company reports -week fiscal year align its fiscal quarters with calendar quarters adding week its first fiscal quarter. All information presented herein based the Company\' fiscal calendar. Financial Instruments Cash Equivalents and Short-term Investments The Company places its short-term investments highly liquid securities issued high credit quality issuers. All highly liquid investments with maturities three months less the date purchase are classified cash equivalents; highly liquid investments with maturities greater than three months are classified short-term investments. Management determines the appropriate classification its investments debt and marketable equity securities the time purchase and reevaluates such designation each balance sheet date. The Company\' debt and marketable equity securities have been classified and accounted for available-for-sale. These securities are carried fair value, with the unrealized gains and losses, net taxes, reported component shareholders\' equity. The cost securities sold based upon the specific identification method. Non-Current Debt and Equity Investments The Company has made investments non-current debt and equity investments public and privately held companies that have been reflected the consolidated balance sheets long-term assets within other assets. They are not categorized current assets either because, given their nature, they are not readily convertible into cash because they represent potentially longer-term investments the Company. Further, the fair value these investments has been subject high degree volatility. The Company\' non-current debt and equity investments have been categorized available-for-sale requiring that they carried fair value with unrealized gains and losses, net taxes, reported equity component accumulated other comprehensive income. However, the Company recognizes impairment charge earnings the event decline fair value below the cost basis one these investments determined other-than-temporary. The Company includes recognized gains and losses resulting from the sale from other-than-temporary declines fair value associated with these investments other income and expense. Occasionally, the Company uses short-term equity derivatives ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]EA1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' manage potential dispositions non-current debt and equity investments. Any gains losses associated with such derivatives are recognized currently other income and expense. Financial Instruments with Characteristics Both Liabilities and Equity May , , the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued Statement Financial Accounting Standards (SFAS) . , Accounting for Certain Financial Instruments with Characteristics Both Liabilities and Equity . SFAS . requires issuers classify liabilities ( assets some circumstances) certain freestanding financial instruments that embody obligations for the issuer and have characteristics both liabilities and equity. The Company adopted the provisions SFAS . June , , which resulted favorable cumulative-effect type adjustment approximately $ million. This adjustment related forward purchase agreement that allowed the Company acquire million shares its common stock average price $ per share for total cost $ million. The Company settled this forward purchase agreement August , which resulted additional gain approximately $ million representing the increase fair value the agreement from June , through the settlement date. Inventories Inventories are stated the lower cost (first- , first-out) market. the cost the inventories exceeds their market value, provisions are made currently for the difference between the cost and the market value. Property, Plant, and Equipment Property, plant, and equipment are stated cost. Depreciation computed use the declining balance and straight-line methods over the estimated useful lives the assets, which are years for buildings, from years for equipment, and the shorter lease terms years for leasehold improvements. The Company capitalizes eligible costs acquire develop internal-use software that are incurred subsequent the preliminary project stage. Capitalized costs related internal-use software are amortized using the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives the assets, which range from years. Asset Retirement Obligations September , , the Company adopted SFAS . , Accounting for Asset Retirement Obligations , which addresses financial accounting and reporting for obligations associated with the retirement tangible long-lived assets and the associated asset retirement costs. The standard applies legal obligations associated with the retirement long-lived assets that result from the acquisition, construction, development and normal use the assets. SFAS . requires that the fair value liability for asset retirement obligation recognized the period which incurred reasonable estimate fair value can made. The fair value the liability added the carrying amount the associated asset and this additional carrying amount depreciated over the life the asset. All the Company\' existing asset retirement obligations are associated with commitments return property subject operating leases original condition upon lease termination. The Company estimated that September , , gross expected future cash flows $ million would required fulfill these obligations. Revenue Recognition Net sales consist primarily revenue from the sale products (hardware, software, and peripherals), and extended warranty and support contracts. The Company recognizes revenue pursuant applicable accounting standards, including Statement Position (SOP) . - , Software Revenue Recognition , amended, and Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Staff Accounting Bulletin (SAB) . , Revenue Recognition Financial Statements . The Company recognizes revenue when persuasive evidence arrangement exists, delivery has occurred, the sales price fixed determinable, and collection probable. Product considered delivered the customer once has been shipped and title and risk loss have been transferred. For most the Company\' product sales, these criteria are met the time the product shipped. For online sales individuals, for some sales education customers the United States, and for certain other sales, the Company defers revenue until the customer receives the product because the Company legally retains portion the risk loss these sales during transit. the outset arrangement the Company determines the arrangement fee not, presumed not , fixed and determinable, revenue deferred and subsequently recognized amounts become due and payable. Revenue from extended warranty and support contracts deferred and recognized ratably over the warranty and support periods. These contracts typically include extended phone support, certain repairs, web-based support resources, diagnostic tools, and extend the Company\' one-year basic limited parts and labor warranty. The Company sells software and peripheral products obtained from other companies. The Company establishes its own pricing and retains related inventory risk, the primary obligor sales transactions with its customers, and assumes the credit risk for amounts billed its customers. Accordingly, the Company recognizes revenue for the sale products obtained from other companies the gross amount billed. Revenue arrangements that include multiple elements such hardware, software, and services allocated each element based vendor specific objective evidence (VSOE) the fair value each element. Allocated revenue for each element recognized when revenue recognition criteria have been met for each element. VSOE determined based the price charged when each element sold separately. The Company records reductions revenue for estimated commitments related price protection and for customer incentive programs, including reseller and end user rebates, and other sales programs and volume-based incentives. The estimated cost these programs accrued reduction revenue the period the Company has sold the product and committed plan. The Company also records reductions revenue for expected future product returns based the Company\' historical experience. Warranty Expense The Company provides currently for the estimated cost for product warranties the time the related revenue recognized. Research and Development Research and development costs are expensed incurred. Development costs computer software sold, leased otherwise marketed are subject capitalization beginning when product\' technological feasibility has been established and ending when product available for general release customers pursuant SFAS . , Computer Software Sold, Leased, Otherwise Marketed . most instances, the Company\' products are released soon after technological feasibility has been established. Therefore, costs incurred subsequent achievement technological feasibility are usually not significant, and generally all software development costs have been expensed. During the third and fourth quarters , the Company incurred substantial development costs associated with the development Mac version (code-named "Panther"), which enhances the features and functionality the previous version Mac , subsequent achievement technological feasibility evidenced public demonstration and release developer beta June , and prior release the final version the product the first quarter . Therefore, during the Company capitalized approximately $ million development costs associated with the development Panther. Amortization this asset began the first quarter when Panther was shipped and being recognized straight-line basis accordance with SFAS . over year estimated useful life. Amortization this asset began the fourth quarter when Jaguar was shipped and being recognized straight-line basis accordance with SFAS . over year estimated useful life. addition, during , the Company also began capitalizing certain costs related development its new PowerSchool enterprise student information system. Capitalization approximately $ million began upon achievement technological feasibility the first quarter . The final version the enterprise student information system was released July . During the Company incurred substantial development costs associated with the development the original version Mac , subsequent release public beta version the product and prior release the final product version. result, the Company capitalized approximately $ million development costs during associated with development Mac . Restructuring Charges June , the FASB issued SFAS . , Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit Disposal Activities . SFAS . supersedes Emerging Issues Task Force (EITF) Issue . - , Liability Recognition for Certain Employee Termination Benefits and Other Costs Exit Activity (Including Certain Costs Associated with Restructuring) and requires that liability for cost associated with exit disposal activity recognized when the liability incurred, opposed when management commits exit plan. SFAS . also establishes that the liability should initially measured and recorded fair value. This Statement was effective for exit disposal activities initiated after December , . The provisions SFAS . were required applied prospectively after the adoption date newly initiated exit activities. Stock-Based Compensation The Company measures compensation expense for its employee stock-based compensation plans using the intrinsic value method prescribed Accounting Principles Board (APB) Opinion . , Accounting for Stock Issued Employees. The Company applies the disclosure provisions SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation , amended SFAS . , Accounting for Stock-based Compensation\x97Transition and Disclosure the fair value-based method had been applied measuring compensation expense. The Company has elected follow APB Opinion . because, discussed below, the alternative fair value accounting provided for under SFAS . requires use option valuation models that were not developed for use valuing employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. Under APB Opinion . , when the exercise price the Company\' employee stock options equals the market price the underlying stock the date the grant, compensation expense recognized. required under SFAS . , the pro forma effects stock-based compensation net income and earnings per common share for employee stock options granted and employee stock purchase plan purchases have been estimated the date grant and beginning the period, respectively, using Black-Scholes option pricing model. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. The Black-Scholes option valuation model was developed for use estimating the fair value freely traded options that have vesting restrictions and are fully transferable. addition, option valuation models require the input highly subjective assumptions including the expected life options and the Company\' expected stock price volatility. Because the Company\' employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares have characteristics significantly different from those freely traded options, and because changes the subjective input assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate, ZEQ.= ,SEQ= ,EFW=" ", ="APPLE COMPUTER, INC.", =" ",CHK= ,FOLIO=\' \',FILE=\'DISK012:[03PAL0 03PAL1910]EA1910A.; \',USER=\'ATOBAK\', =\' -DEC- ; : \' management\' opinion, the existing models not provide reliable measure the fair value the Company\' employee stock options and employee stock purchase plan shares. For purposes pro forma disclosures, the estimated fair value the options and shares amortized pro forma net income (loss) over the options\' vesting period and the shares\' plan period. Comprehensive Income Comprehensive income consists two components, net income and other comprehensive income. Other comprehensive income refers revenue, expenses, gains and losses that under generally accepted accounting principles are recorded element shareholders\' equity but are excluded from net income. The Company\' other comprehensive income comprised foreign currency translation adjustments from those subsidiaries not using the . dollar their functional currency, unrealized gains and losses marketable securities categorized available-for-sale, and net deferred gains and losses certain derivative instruments accounted for cash flow hedges. Information about the Company\' products, major customers, and geographic areas company-wide basis also disclosed. Foreign Exchange Risk Management The Company enters into foreign currency forward and option contracts with financial institutions primarily protect against foreign exchange risk associated with existing assets and liabilities, certain firmly committed transactions and certain probable but not firmly committed transactions. Generally, the Company\' practice hedge majority its existing material foreign exchange transaction exposures. However, the Company may not hedge certain foreign exchange transaction exposures due immateriality, prohibitive economic cost hedging particular exposures, limited availability appropriate hedging instruments. Interest Rate Risk Management The Company sometimes enters into interest rate derivative transactions, including interest rate swaps, collars, and floors, with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income its cash equivalents and short-term investments with its fixed-rate interest expense its long-term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short-term . interest rates. September , , the Company had entered into interest rate swaps with financial institutions order better match the Company\' floating-rate interest income its cash equivalents and short-term investments with its fixed-rate interest expense its long-term debt, and diversify portion the Company\' exposure away from fluctuations short-term . interest rates. Contingencies Beginning September , , three shareholder class action lawsuits were filed the United States District Court for the Northern District California against the Company and its Chief Executive Officer. These lawsuits are substantially identical, and purport bring suit behalf persons who purchased the Company\' publicly traded common stock between July , , and September , . The complaints allege violations the Securities Exchange Act and seek unspecified compensatory damages and other relief. The Company believes these claims are without merit and intends defend them vigorously. The Company filed motion dismiss June , , which was heard the Court September , . December , , the Court granted the Company\' motion dismiss for failure state cause action, with leave Plaintiffs amend their complaint within thirty days. Plaintiffs filed their amended complaint January , , and March , , the Company filed motion dismiss the amended complaint. The Court heard the Company\' motion July , and dismissed Plaintiff\' claims with prejudice August , . Plaintiffs have appealed the ruling. The Company subject certain other legal proceedings and claims that have arisen the ordinary course business and have not been fully adjudicated. the opinion management, the Company does not have potential liability related any current legal proceedings and claims that would individually the aggregate have material adverse effect its financial condition, liquidity results operations. However, the results legal proceedings cannot predicted with certainty. Should the Company fail prevail any these legal matters should several these legal matters resolved against the Company the same reporting period, the operating results particular reporting period could materially adversely affected. Note \x97Segment Information and Geographic Data The Company manages its business primarily geographic basis. The Company\' reportable segments are comprised the Americas, Europe, Japan, and Retail. The Americas segment includes both North and South America, except for the activities the Company\' Retail segment. The Europe segment includes European countries well the Middle East and Africa. The Japan segment includes only Japan. September , , the Retail segment currently operates Apple-owned retail stores the United States. Other operating segments include Asia-Pacific, which includes Australia and Asia except for Japan, and the Company\' subsidiary, Filemaker, Inc. Each reportable operating segment provides similar hardware and software products and similar services, and the accounting policies the various segments are the same those described the Summary Significant Accounting Policies Note , except described below for the Retail segment. The Company evaluates the performance its operating segments based net sales. The Retail segment\' performance also evaluated based operating income. Net sales for geographic segments are based the location the customers. Operating income for each segment includes net sales third parties, related cost sales, and operating expenses directly attributable the segment. Operating income for each segment excludes other income and expense and certain expenses that are managed outside the operating segments. Costs excluded from segment operating income include various corporate expenses, manufacturing costs not included standard costs, income taxes, and various nonrecurring charges. Corporate expenses include research and development, corporate marketing expenses, and other separately managed general and administrative expenses including certain corporate expenses associated with support the Retail segment. The Company does not include intercompany transfers between segments for management reporting purposes. Segment assets exclude corporate assets. Corporate assets include cash, short-term and long-term investments, manufacturing facilities, miscellaneous corporate infrastructure, goodwill and other acquired intangible assets, and retail store construction- -progress that not subject depreciation. Except for the Retail segment, capital expenditures for long-lived assets are not reported management segment. Capital expenditures the Retail segment were $ million, $ million, and $ million , , and , respectively. Operating income for all segments except Retail includes cost sales standard cost.
